   {"@context":"http://schema.org","headline":"1898: Portraits of Native Americans from 'Buffalo Bill's Wild West' show","url":"http://mashable.com/2015/02/18/native-american-portraits/","image":"http://rack.0.mshcdn.com/media/ZgkyMDE1LzAyLzE4L2FiL0J1ZmZhbG9CaWxsLmFiNTcxLmpwZwpwCXRodW1iCTEyMDB4NjI3IwplCWpwZw/3078a3f5/937/Buffalo-Bills-performers-201.jpg","keywords":["features","history","u.s.","uncategorized","us-world","us","travel-leisure","retronaut","native-american","wild-west"],"@type":"Article","dateCreated":"2015-02-18T19:39:22Z","datePublished":"2015-02-18T19:39:22Z","articleSection":"world","creator":"Chris Wild","author":"Chris Wild","articleBody":"Iron White Man\nImage: Library of Congress\nIn 1898, photographer Gertrude K\u00e4sebier looked out of her\u00a0studio window on Fifth Avenue in New York City and saw\u00a0the cast of Buffalo Bill's Wild West\u00a0parading past.\u00a0Buffalo Bill, a.k.a. William Cody, was by that time a legendary figure of the American Old West, a legend he partially self-generated. Cody's nickname arrived when he supplied buffalo meat to workers on the Kansas Pacific railroad.\nIn 1872, Cody performed in the Wild West theatre production Scouts of the Prairie, and in 1883, aged 37, he founded his own circus-like\u00a0show, called\u00a0Buffalo Bill's Wild West. The show toured annually across the U.S. and Europe, performing in front of Queen Victoria and the future kings Edward VII and George V of Britain, and the future Kaiser Wilhelm II of Germany. In Rome, the cast met the pope.\nThe show included sharpshooting acts, horseriding demonstrations and reenactments of American history. The performers included several Native Americans, many of them Sioux.\nWhat\u00a0Gertrude K\u00e4sebier saw from her window connected with her\u00a0memories of the Native Americans she had known in the 1850s and 1860s, growing up in Colorado and on the Great Plains.\u00a0K\u00e4sebier\u00a0wrote to Cody asking if she might photograph\u00a0the Native American performers in her studio. They arranged a session.\u00a0\nA number of the Sioux photographed had fought against the U.S. military. Chief Flying Hawk was a veteran of Great Sioux War of 1876, the Battle of the Little Big Horn of the same year and was present at the massacre of Wounded Knee \u2014 just eight years before\u00a0K\u00e4sebier took his portrait.\n\nFlying Hawk\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nFlying Hawk\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nFlying Hawk\nImage: Library of Congress\nDear Mr. Cody,\nI have seen your Wild West show two days in succession, and have enjoyed it thoroughly.It brought vividly back the breezy wild life of the Great Plains and the Rocky Mountains, and stirred me like a war-song. \nTruly yours,\nMark Twain\nLetter to Buffalo Bill Cody,  Sep. 10, 1884\n\nJoe Black Fox\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nJoe Black Fox\nImage: Library of Congress\nI thought I was benefiting the Indians as well as the government, by taking them all over the United States, and giving them a correct idea of the customs, and life of the pale faces, so that when they returned to their people they could make known all they had seen.\n\nWilliam Cody\n\nJoe Black Fox\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWhirling Horse\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWhirling Horse\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWhirling Horse\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWhirling Hawk\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nCharging Thunder\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nCharging Thunder\nImage: Library of of Congress\n\nAmerican Horse and wife\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nAmerican Horse and wife\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nAmerican Horse\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWife of American Horse\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nShooting Pieces\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nSammy Lone Bear\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nSammy Lone Bear\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nLuke Big Turnips\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWhirlwind Horse\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nPlenty Wounds\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWilliam Frog\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nAmos Little\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nHoly Frog(?) (left) and Big Turnips(?)\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nBad Bear\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nTakes Enemy\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nUnidentified man\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nWhite War Bonnet\nImage: Library of Congress\n\nKills Close to the Lodge\nImage: Library of Congress\n              Share this story                              Share                Tweet                                                                                          \n\nText and curation:\nAmanda Uren\n","mainEntityOfPage":"True","metadata":{"page":1,"omnitureData":{"channel":"world","content_type":"article","v_buy":null,"v_buy_i":null,"h_pub":3482.0,"h_buy":null,"h_pub_buy":null,"v_cur":4.7,"v_max":4.7,"v_cur_i":4,"v_max_i":4,"events":"event52,event61,event62","top_channel":"world","content_source_type":"Internal - Editorial Series","content_source_name":"edit-retronaut","author_name":"Chris Wild","age":"145","pub_day":18,"pub_month":2,"pub_year":2015,"pub_date":"02/18/2015","sourced_from":"Internal","isPostView":true,"post_lead_type":"Longform","topics":"features,History,native american,Retronaut,Travel,Travel &amp; Leisure,U.S.,Uncategorized,U.S.,World,wild west","campaign":null,"display_mode":null,"viral_video_type":null,"b_flag":true},"postId":3242091}}

1898, photographer Gertrude K\u00e4sebier looked out of her&nbsp;studio window on Fifth Avenue in New York City and saw&nbsp;the cast of &lt;i&gt;Buffalo Bill's Wild West&lt;/i&gt;&nbsp;parading past.&nbsp;Buffalo Bill, a.k.a. William Cody, was by that time a legendary figure of the American Old West, a legend he partially self-generated. Cody's nickname arrived when he supplied buffalo meat to workers on the Kansas Pacific railroad.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In 1872, Cody performed in the Wild West theatre production &lt;i&gt;Scouts of the Prairie&lt;/i&gt;, and in 1883, aged 37, he founded his own circus-like&nbsp;show, called&nbsp;&lt;i style=\&quot;font-size: 1.7rem;\&quot;&gt;Buffalo Bill's Wild West&lt;/i&gt;. The show toured annually across the U.S. and Europe, performing in front of Queen Victoria and the future kings Edward VII and George V of Britain, and the future Kaiser Wilhelm II of Germany. In Rome, the cast met the pope.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The show included sharpshooting acts, horseriding demonstrations and reenactments of American history. The performers included several Native Americans, many of them Sioux.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;What&nbsp;Gertrude K\u00e4sebier saw from her window connected with her&nbsp;memories of the Native Americans she had known in the 1850s and 1860s, growing up in Colorado and on the Great Plains.&nbsp;K\u00e4sebier&nbsp;wrote to Cody asking if she might photograph&nbsp;the Native American performers in her studio. They arranged a session.&nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A number of the Sioux photographed had fought against the U.S. military. Chief Flying Hawk was a veteran of Great Sioux War of 1876, the Battle of the Little Big Horn of the same year and was present at the massacre of Wounded Knee \u2014 just eight years before&nbsp;K\u00e4sebier took his portrait.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;],&quot;extended_options&quot;:{},&quot;id&quot;:&quot;54e4b83a31829706c002b453&quot;,&quot;id_string&quot;:&quot;19eec6mqs19eec6mrckncs&quot;,&quot;template&quot;:&quot;ChapterTextTemplate&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:[],&quot;version&quot;:&quot;0&quot;},{&quot;content&quot;:[&quot;&quot;,&quot;Flying Congress&lt;/a&gt;&quot;],&quot;extended_options&quot;:{&quot;native_width&quot;:&quot;1200&quot;,&quot;native_height&quot;:&quot;1557&quot;},&quot;id&quot;:&quot;54e4b83a31829706c002b456&quot;,&quot;id_string&quot;:&quot;19ee88tnl19ee88tnvn429&quot;,&quot;template&quot;:&quot;InfographicTemplate&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:[&quot;http://1.mshcdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Buffalo-Bills-performers-1.jpg&quot;],&quot;version&quot;:&quot;0&quot;},{&quot;content&quot;:[&quot;Dear Mr. Cody,&lt;br&gt;\n&lt;br&gt;I have seen your Wild West show two days in succession, and have enjoyed it thoroughly.&lt;br&gt;It brought vividly back the breezy wild life of the Great Plains and the Rocky Mountains, and stirred me like a war-song.&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt; \nTruly yours,&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;\nMark Twain&quot;,&quot;Letter to Buffalo Bill Cody,  Sep. 10,         <div class="parsec-block parsec-block-text " data-style='{"width":"20em"}' data-type="TextBlock" style="width: 20em">
         <div class="title-text">
          <p class="date">
           c. 1898
          </p>
          <p class="headline">
           Native Americans from
           <br/>
           "Buffalo Bill's Wild West"
          </p>
          <p class="subheadline" style="width:30em;">
           Portraits of the men and women who performed for Queen Victoria
          </p>
          <p class="author">
           <a href="http://www.retronaut.com" target="_blank">
            by Amanda Uren
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="retronaut-logo">
           <a href="http://mashable.com/category/retronaut" target="_blank">
            <img src="/assets/parsec/Retronaut.Logo.gif"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>

       <div class="long-card parsec-card image-card infographic-card v0" data-breakpoint="[&quot;x\x9CM\x90\xCBN\xC30\x10E\x7Fe\x94\x15E\xAD\x1D\xE7E\x9B5\x12[\x04\xDBJ\x91\x9DL\x13\v\xC7)\xB6\x93P!\xFE\x9Dq)\b\xAFf|\xE7q\xE6~&amp;'\xD9j\xA3\xC3%\xA9\x93\x17\xA9\x8D\x87\xBBg7us\e\xF4d7\xC96Y\xD0y\nI\x16,\xA5|\x98|\xA0dE%\xD8(\xFD \x95A\xD6N#I\x06\x174I]m\x13?L.4#z/{\xA4\xEA\xA3\xBD\x8F\x0F\x1EQ\xCD}\x8F\x0E\x1C\xBE\xCF\xE8\x03v[Ps\x80Uz\xB0S\x00\xB9\x10B\x9C\bwh\xFD\xEC\x10\xDC\xAC.\xBB.\xB6\x81\xF6`t\xEC\x01m\xE1\t\xC7\x936\xC8\xB5\xF5A\x1AC\x9F4\xA2\xC7qS\xC3k\x90.\x80GG\xE8\xB0\xEA0\xC0\xEEgB\\\x1C&amp;@{\xDDp%:Z\xE2\xBE\xC14\xBA#\xD44\x13\xD5\x83Ri\xD1\xC9\xB6,\x8BS\xDA\x15e\x81\x87,\x17R\xE4\xA2*\xA8&gt;.\xA6J\xBEH\xC7\xD7u\xE5K\xF4\xC4\xF3\xFFn\xFC%\xCD\x92q\x8A\x1Cv\\\xCD\xB6#\xE2x\x11\xCFX\xCARN\xBC\x9EK\xB2zA?\x9F\xCF\xE4\xD9.g\x19\x13{n\xB4\xBA\t\xCDM\xE1\xED\xE4\xB0\xC1\x8F\xC0\xDF\xD0Y4\xFC\xF7$\xE6T\xF4^[\xBCZ\x1F4\xD9\x1E\xE4xNjQ\xE4\xD5&gt;\xCB\x0F\xD5\x81U\x99H\xAB\xF2\xEB\e\xD6\xA0\xA5E&quot;]" data-chapter="" data-chapter-fragment="" data-chapter-image="" data-extended-options="{}" data-height-style="" data-style="{}" data-title="Card" data-type="LongCard" id="" style="">
        <div class="parsec-block parsec-block-image infographic-block image-wrap" data-click-through-url="" data-native-height="1552" data-native-width="1200" data-type="ImageBlock" data-url="http://1.mshcdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Buffalo-Bills-performers-28.jpg">

         <p class="title">
         </p>
         <p class="caption">
          Iron White Man
         </p>
         <p class="credit">
          Image:
          <a href="http://www.loc.gov/pictures/related/?va=exact&amp;sp=1&amp;st=gallery&amp;pk=2006679586&amp;sb=call_number&amp;sg=true&amp;op=EQUAL">
           Library of Congress

       <div class="long-card parsec-card text-card v0 text-center" data-breakpoint="[&quot;x\x9CM\x90\xCBN\xC30\x10E\x7Fe\xE4\x15E\xAD\x9D7M\xD7Hl\x11l+Ev2M,\x1C\xA7\xD8NB\x85\xF8w\xC6\xA5 \xBC\x9A\xF1\x9D\xC7\x99\xFB\xC9N\xB2\xD5F\x87\v;\xB0\x17\xA9\x8D\x87\xBBg7us\e\xF4d7l\xCB\x16t\x9EB\x92S\x9EP&gt;L&gt;P\xB2\xA2J\xF9(\xFD \x95A\xDEN#I\x06\x174\xECPm\x99\x1F&amp;\x17\x9A\x11\xBD\x97=R\xF5\xD1\xDE\xC7\a\x8F\xA8\xE6\xBEG\a\x0E\xDFg\xF4\x01\xBB-\xA89\xC0*=\xD8)\x80\\\b!N\x84;\xB4~v\bnV\x97]\x17\xDB@{0:\xF6\x80\xB6\xF0\x84\xE3I\e\x14\xDA\xFA \x8D\xA1O\x1A\xD1\xE3\xB89\xC0k\x90.\x80GG\xE8\xB0\xEA0\xC0\xEEgB\\\x1C&amp;@{\xDDp%:Z\xE2\xBE\xC14\xBA#\xD4$K\xAB\a\xA5\x92\xA2\x93mY\x16\xA7\xA4+\xCA\x02\xEB,Oe\x9A\xA7UA\xF5q1U\x8AE:\xB1\xAE\xABX\xA2'^\xFCw\xE3/i\x96LP\xE4\xB0\x13j\xB6\x1D\x11\xC7\x8BD\xC6\x13\x9E\b\xE2\xF5B\x92\xD5\v\xFA\xF9|&amp;\xCFv9\xCFx\xBA\x17F\xAB\x9B\xD0\xDC\x14\xD1N\x0E\e\xFC\b\xE2\r\x9DE#~O\xE2NE\xEF\xB5\xC5\xAB\xF5A\x93\xEDA\x8EgvH\x8B\xBC\xDAgy]\xD5\xBC\xCA\xCA\xA4.\xBF\xBE\x01\xD6\xBD\xA5L&quot;]" data-chapter="" data-chapter-fragment="" data-chapter-image="" data-extended-options="{}" data-height-style="" data-style="{}" data-title="Card" data-type="LongCard" id="" style="">
        <div class="parsec-block parsec-block-text text-wrap" data-style="{}" data-type="TextBlock" style="">
         <p>
          In 1898, photographer Gertrude Ksebier looked out of herstudio window on Fifth Avenue in New York City and sawthe cast of
          <i>
           Buffalo Bill's Wild West
          </i>
          parading past.Buffalo Bill, a.k.a. William Cody, was by that time a legendary figure of the American Old West, a legend he partially self-generated. Cody's nickname arrived when he supplied buffalo meat to workers on the Kansas Pacific railroad.
         </p>
         <p>
          In 1872, Cody performed in the Wild West theatre production
          <i>
           Scouts of the Prairie
          </i>
          , and in 1883, aged 37, he founded his own circus-likeshow, called
          <i style="font-size: 1.7rem;">
           Buffalo Bill's Wild West
          </i>
          . The show toured annually across the U.S. and Europe, performing in front of Queen Victoria and the future kings Edward VII and George V of Britain, and the future Kaiser Wilhelm II of Germany. In Rome, the cast met the pope.
         </p>
         <p>
          The show included sharpshooting acts, horseriding demonstrations and reenactments of American history. The performers included several Native Americans, many of them Sioux.
         </p>
         <p>
          WhatGertrude Ksebier saw from her window connected with hermemories of the Native Americans she had known in the 1850s and 1860s, growing up in Colorado and on the Great Plains.Ksebierwrote to Cody asking if she might photographthe Native American performers in her studio. They arranged a session.
         </p>
         <p>
          A number of the Sioux photographed had fought against the U.S. military. Chief Flying Hawk was a veteran of Great Sioux War of 1876, the Battle of the Little Big Horn of the same year and was present at the massacre of Wounded Knee  just eight years beforeKsebier took his portrait.
         </p>
        </div>
       </div>

        <div class="parsec-block parsec-block-image infographic-block image-wrap" data-click-through-url="" data-native-height="1545" data-native-width="1200" data-type="ImageBlock" data-url="http://1.mshcdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Buffalo-Bills-performers-9.jpg">

         <p class="title">
         </p>
         <p class="caption">
          Flying Hawk
         </p>
         <p class="credit">
          Image:
          <a href="http://www.loc.gov/pictures/related/?va=exact&amp;sp=1&amp;st=gallery&amp;pk=2006679586&amp;sb=call_number&amp;sg=true&amp;op=EQUAL">

        <div class="parsec-block parsec-block-text text-wrap" data-style="{}" data-type="TextBlock" style="">
         <div class="quote-content">
          Dear Mr. Cody,
          <br/>
          <br/>
          I have seen your Wild West show two days in succession, and have enjoyed it thoroughly.
          <br/>
          It brought vividly back the breezy wild life of the Great Plains and the Rocky Mountains, and stirred me like a war-song.
          <br/>
          <br/>
          Truly yours,
          <br/>
          <br/>
          Mark Twain
         </div>
         <div class="attribution">
          Letter to Buffalo Bill Cody,  Sep. 10, 1884
         </div>
        </div>

         <div class="quote-content">
          I thought I was benefiting the Indians as well as the government, by taking them all over the United States, and giving them a correct idea of the customs, and life of the pale faces, so that when they returned to their people they could make known all they had seen.
         </div>

          William Cody
